It maintains a count of the occurrences of the current majority candidate and updates it as it iterates through the array. This approach is consistent with the algorithm's logic and ensures that the majority element is identified by the end of the iteration. Moreover, it provides the correct time and space complexity for the algorithm, which is O(n) and O(1) respectively.  Output (b), however, does not implement the Boyer-Moore Voting Algorithm. Instead, it iterates through the array and updates the majority element if the current element is greater than the current majority element. This approach does not find the majority element as it does not account for the frequency of occurrence of elements in the array. It simply selects the largest element in the array, which is not the goal of the Boyer-Moore Voting Algorithm.
